nothing appear in history similar to the enthusiasm rouse by kossuth in nation foreign to he except perhaps the kindling for the first crusade by the voice of peter the hermit then bishop prince and people alike understand the danger which overshadow europe from the mohammedan power and by soundly direct though fanatical instinct all christendom rush eastward till the chivalry of the seljuk turk be cripple on the field of palestine now also the multitude of europe uncorrupted by ambition envy or filthy lucre forebode the deadly struggle impend over we all from the conspiracy of crown head see the apathy of they own ruler and know perhaps by dim report the deed of kossuth they look to he as the great prophet and leader by whom policy be at length to be mould into justice and be ready to catch he inspiration before he have utter a word kossuth undoubtedly be a mighty orator but no one be better aware than he that the cogency of he argument be due to the atrocity of we common enemy and the enthusiasm which he kindle to the preparation of the people 's heart he oration be a tropical forest full of strength and majesty tangled in luxuriance a wilderness of self-repetition utterly unsuited to form a book without immense abridgment they contain material adapt equally for immediate political service and for permanence as a work of wisdom and of genius to prepare they for the press be a arduous and responsible duty : the best excuse which i can give for have assume it be that it have be to I a labor of love my task i have feel to be that of a judicious reporter who cut short what be of temporary interest condense what be too amplify for he limit and for written style severely prune down the repetition which be inevitable where numerous -lrb- \* -rrb- audience be address by the same man on the same subject yet amid all these necessary liberty retain not only the true sentiment and argument of the speaker but he form of thought and all that be characteristic of he genius such a operation rightly perform may like a diminish mirror concentrate the brilliancy of diffuse oration and assist they efficacy on mind which would faint under the effort of grasp the original -lrb- footnote \* : the number of speech great and small speak in he american half-year be reckon to be above 500 -rrb- it be true the exuberance of kossuth be often too asiatic for english taste and that excision of word which needful abridgment suggest will often seem to we a gain moreover remember that he be a foreigner and though marvellous in he mastery of we language still naturally often unable to seize the word or select the construction which he desire i have not think i should show honor to he by retain anything verbally unskilful to a certain cautious extent i account myself to be a _ translator _ as well as a _ reporter _ and in undertake so delicate a duty i be happy to announce that i have receive kossuth 's write approval and thanks mere quaintness of expression i have by no means desire entirely to remove where it involve nothing grotesque obscure or monotonous in several passage where i imperfectly understand the thought i have have the advantage of kossuth 's personal explanation which have enable I to clear up the defective report or real obscurity of he word nevertheless i have to confess my conviction that nothing can wholly compensate for the want of systematic revision by the author himself which he great occupation have make impossible the mistake in the report of the speech be sometimes rather subtle and have not rouse my suspicion of this i have be make disagreeably sensible by several erratum communicate to I by kossuth in the first great speech at new york here mark as no vii -lrb- which have be correct in this edition -rrb- nearly all the point on which attempt have be make to misrepresent in england the cause of hungary be clear up in these speech on two subject only do it seem needful here to make any remark : _ first _ on the republicanism of kossuth _ secondly _ on the hungarian levy against italy in the year 1848 1 kossuth be attack by he countryman on opposite grounds : szemerè despise he for not become a republican early enough count casimir bathyanyus reprove he for become a republican at all the fact be these kossuth like all english statesman be a historical royalist not a doctrinaire when the exist reign have become treacherous and lawless he be willing to change the line of succession and make the archduke stephen king when the dynasty have become universally detest and actually expel he approve most heartily -lrb- \* -rrb- the deposition of the hapsburg but still hold himself in suspense as to the future of the constitution by he influence instruction be send to he representative in england which be equivalent to solicit a dynasty from the british government meanwhile szemerè he home secretary take on himself to avow in the diet that the government be republican and no voice of protest be raise in either house indeed mr vucovic who be minister of justice under kossuth state -lrb- see appendix i -rrb- that the government and both house respond unanimously to the republican avowal and that the government remove the symbol of the crown from the public arm and seal the press of all shades assent after this it be clear -lrb- i presume -rrb- to kossuth or at least it soon become so that all sympathy with royal power be go out of the nation 's heart hungarian may settle that amongst themselves : but as for englishman -- when for seven or eight month together the english ministry and english peerage would not stir or speak or whisper to save constitutional royalty and ancient peerage for hungary and for europe while it be yet possible with what face with what decency can englishmen censure kossuth for despair of a cause which be abandon to ruin by ourselves the greatest power interested to maintain it -- which the monarch have wade through blood and perjury to destroy-and which the million of hungary will not -lrb- in he belief -rrb- peril life and fortune to restore -lrb- footnote \* : how unanimous be the whole country be clear by the fact state how spontaneous be the movement and free from all government intrigue see in appendix i this be entirely confirm by we envoy mr blackwell : blue book march -- ap 1848 -rrb- 2 the ministry of loui bathyanyus and kossuth have be attack on opposite grounds -- because they _ do _ and because they do _ not _ attempt to subdue the italian by force of arm the fact be rather complicate but deserve here to be state concisely when the ministry be appoint there be _ already _ hungarian in italy with radetzkus and austrian soldier in hungary the viennese ministry promise to exchange they as fast as could be do without encounter great expense or dislocate the regiment and make they inefficient with this promise the hungarian ministry be force to content itself at the time at a later period when it discover that the austrian commander in hungary have secret order not to fight against the serbian marauder and that the austrian troops could not be trust the hungarian ministry _ desire _ to get back they man from italy for they own defense which desire prove ineffectual yet have be severely blame by some of we monarchist but meanwhile the viennese ministry as early as June 1848 endeavor to buy of the hungarian ministry a increase grant of troops against italy by concede a most energetic king 's speech against the serb with which the archduke palatine be to open and do open the diet on July 2d a part of this speech be quote in appendix ii and indeed it be a loathsome exhibition of austrian treachery the hungarian ministry be press by the argument that since austrium be attack in italy by the king of sardinium the war be not merely against the lombard and that the pragmatic sanction bind hungary to defend the empire if assail from without this lead they to acknowledge the _ principle _ that they be bind to assist if able but they reply that hungary itself must first be secure against marauder and no troops could be spare until the serb be subdue at the same time order be send to radetzki from vienna to offer independence to the lombard and constitutional nationality under the austrian crown to the venetian : hence the hungarian ministry for a time fancy that they would not be fight against the italian as they expect the term to be accept by they when it be farther represent that the italian have reject they -- -lrb- for radetzkus act probably by secret order suppress the despatch and never offer independence to lombardy though the austrian minister make diplomatic capital of they liberality -rrb- -- then the hungarian ministry begin to think the italian unreasonable yet they do not go beyond they abstract principle that hungary ought to grant troops for austrian defense in italy provide 1st that rebellion in hungary itself be repress 2d that the troops should not act against the italian unless the italian have reject the offer of national liberty and a constitution coordinate to those of hungary under the austrian crown the protocol on this subject be draw on July 5th the public speech of kossuth concern it be not until July 22d and in this short interval the treachery of the dynasty have be so display that kossuth could no longer speak in the same tone as a few week earlier for a fuller development of this i refer the reader to appendix iii the real object of the austrian ministry be to ruin the popularity of bathyanyus and kossuth if they could induce they to sacrifice italian freedom or else to accuse they to all the european diplomatist as conspirator against the integrity of the austrian empire if they refuse to oppress the liberty of italy finally the reader have even here proof enough how false be the statement which have be current in english newspaper that kossuth 's visit to america be a failure this be a attempt to practice on we prevalent disgraceful tendency to judge of a cause by its success however the end be not yet see : america have still to act decisively if she would win the lasting glory which we have future of nation new york appendix kossuth 's speech -lrb- the speech of kossuth in england though masterly in themselves be in great measure supersede by those which he deliver in america where the same subject be treat at far greater length and view from many different aspect from the speech in england i here present only three topic in a rather fragmentary form -rrb- i -- secrecy of diplomacy -lrb- _ first extract : from kossuth 's speech at the guildhall london oct 30th _ 1851 -rrb- the time draw near when a radical change must take place for the whole world in the management of diplomacy its basis have be secrecy : therein be the triumph of absolutism and the misfortune of a free people this have win its way not in england only but throughout the whole world even where not a penny of the national property can be dispose of without public consent it surely be dangerous to the interest of the country and to constitutional liberty to allow such a secrecy that the people not only should not know how its interest be be deal with but that after the crisis be pass the minister should inform they : the dinner have be prepare -- and eat and the people have nothing to do but digest the consequence what be the principle of all evil in europe the encroach spirit of russium -- and by what power have russia become so mighty by its arm -- no : the arm of russium be below those of many power it have become almost omnipotent -- at least very dangerous to liberty -- by diplomatic intrigue now against the secret intrigue of diplomacy there be no surer safeguard or more powerful counteraction than public discussion this must be oppose to intrigue and intrigue be then of no weight in the destiny of humanity \* \* \* \* \* -lrb- _ second extract from a short speech in london may 25th 1858 _ -rrb- i must ask leave to make a remark on the system pursue by you government in they foreign relation you consider yourselve a constitutional nation : i fear that in some respects you be not so there be a latin proverb -lrb- current in hungary -rrb- _ nil de nobis sine nobis _ -- nothing that concern we without we this in many thing you make you maxim you say that none of you money shall be spend without you knowledge and approval and in you internal affair you carry this out but i think that the secrecy in which the transaction of you diplomacy be involve be hardly constitutional of that most important portion of you affair which concern you country in its relation with the rest of europe what knowledge have you if any interpellation be make about any affair not yet conclude my lord the secretary of the foreign office will reply that _ he can not give any answer for the negotiation be still pend _ a little later he will be able to answer that _ as all be now conclude all comment will be superfluous _ one little fact i will just mention by the last treaty with denmark to which you become a party the crown of that kingdom be so settle that only three life stand between it and the czar of russium three life but a fragile barrier when high political aim be concern it be therefore a allow fact that the country which command entrance to the baltic and which in the hand of a unfriendly power would effectually exclude you commerce from that sea may pass into the hand of russium whose pretension in the south of europe you take so much pain to check this you government have do quietly how many be there of you people that know and approve it i hope you will not be offend if i say that i can not understand how yours can be call in this respect a constitutional country \* \* \* \* \* ii -- monarchy and republicanism -lrb- _ from kossuth 's speech at copenhagen house nov 3d 1851 _ -rrb- in my opinion the form of government may be different in different country accord to they circumstance they wish they want england love she queen and have full motive to do so england feel great glorious and free and have full reason to feel so but the fact of england be a monarchy can not be sufficient reason for she to hate and discredit republican form of government in other country differ in circumstance in wish and in want on the other side to the united state of america which under republican government be likewise great glorious and free they republicanism give no sufficient reason to hate and discredit monarchical government in england it entirely belong to the right of every nation to dispose of its domestic concern therefore i claim for my own country also that england see from we past that we cause be just should profess the sovereign right of every nation to dispose of itself and should allow no power whatever to interfere with we domestic matter since i thus regard the internal affair of every nation to be its own separate concern i do not think it become I here in england to speak about the future organization of we country but my behavior have not be everywhere appreciate as i hope i have meet in certain quarter the remark that i be slippery and evade the question now on the point of sincerity i be particularly susceptible i have the sentiment of be a straightforward man and i would not be charge with have steal into the sympathy of england without display my true color therefore i must clearly state that in we past struggle it be not _ we _ who make a revolution we begin peacefully and legislatively to transform the monarchico-aristocratical constitution of hungary into a monarchico-democratical constitution we preserve we municipal institution as we most valuable treasure but to they as well as to the legislative power we give as basis the common liberty of the people instead of the class-privilege of old moreover in place of the old board of council -- which be a corporate body be of course a mockery in regard to that responsibility of the executive which be we chartered right on paper -- we establish the real and personal responsibility of minister in this we merely -lrb- \* -rrb- uphold what be due to we by constitution by treaty by the coronation-oath of every king -- the right to be govern as a self-consistent independent country by we native institution accord to we own law this and all we other reform we effect peacefully by careful legislation which the king sanction and swear to maintain -lrb- footnote \* : many englishman have unjustly accuse the hungarian as have by the law of march 1848 effect a separation of hungary from austria _ even if this be true _ it could not justify the cause of the hapsburg the dynasty yield under the pressure of circumstance -lrb- as alone will dynasty ever yield -rrb- while hungary do but petition legally and be in fact unarm the dynasty swear to the new law and then conspire with croatian serbian and russian to overthrow the law by maraud and force of arm in fact if in January 1849 austrium would have negotiate instead of arrest all hungarian ambassador hungary would have consent to modify the law of march : but the austrian have already in October order the overthrow of the whole hungarian constitution and have no wish to do anything by legal method at the same time the original objection be fundamentally _ false _ no separation of the two country be effect by the law of march 1848 for no legal union ever exist only the crown be unite not the country kossuth rightly compare the union to that which be between england and hanover at any time in the past hungary might have make _ peace _ with a power with which austrium be at _ war _ if the king have not falsify they oath by not assemble the diet : for the diet always have the lawful right of war and peace any mode whatsoever of enforce the coronation oath might accord to this logic be condemn as a separate of austrium and hungary -rrb- nevertheless this very dynasty in the most perjurious manner attack these law this freedom this constitution by arm we defend ourselves by arm victoriously when upon this the perjurious dynasty call in the russian army to beat we down we of course declare the hapsburg to be no longer we sovereign we avow ourselves to be a free and independent nation but fix as yet no definite form of government -- neither monarchical nor republican these be plain fact hungary be not now under lawful government but be be trample down by a foreign intruder who be _ not _ king of hungary be _ neither acknowledge by the nation nor sanction by law _ hungary be in a word in a state of war against the hapsburg dynasty a war of legitimate defense by which alone it can ever regain independence and freedom by such war alone have any nation ever win its freedom from oppressor as you see in switzerland belgium spain portugal france sweden norway greece the united state and england itself i can state it as know to I with the certainty of matter of fact that hungary will never accept the hapsburg as legitimate sovereign in the future nor ever enter into any new moral relation with that perjurious family nor only so but they perjury have so entirely pluck out of my nation 's heart all faith in monarchy and all attachment to it that there be no power on earth to knit the broken tie again : and therefore hungary wish and will to be a free and independent republic -- a republic found on the rule of law secure social order guarantee person property the moral development as well as material welfare of the people -- in a word a republic like that of the united state found on institution inherit from england itself this be the conviction of my people which i share in the very heart of my heart \* \* \* \* \* iii -- communism and the sibylline book -lrb- _ from kossuth 's second speech at manchester nov 12th _ 1851 -rrb- i can understand communism but not socialism i have read many book on the subject i have consult many doctor but they differ so much that i never could understand what they really mean however the only sense which i can see in socialism be inconsistent with social order and the security of property now since france have three time in sixty year fail to obtain practical result from political revolution all europe be apt to press forward into new social doctrine to regulate the future believe then that -- not from my merit but from the state of my country -- i may be able somewhat to influence the course of the next european revolution i think it right plainly to declare beforehand my allegiance to the great principle of security for personal property nevertheless to give success to my endeavor in this direction the rational expectation of the nation of europe must speedily be fulfil else neither i nor more important man can avail to stay revolutionary movement the danger of the case may be illustrate by the ancient story of the sibylline book take hungary as a instance three year ago we should have be extremely well contented with the law as make by we parliament in 1848 _ which law do not break the tie between we and the house of hapsburg _ but then austrium assail we with arm and it become impossible for we to go on with that constitution indeed she herself proclaim it to be dissolve we defeat she and next she call in the russian army hungary be then under the necessity of _ casting off the hapsburg monarchy _ and only the third sibylline book remain yet hungary do not even then renounce monarchy but give instruction to she representative in england to say to the government of this country that _ if they wish to see monarchy establish in hungary we would accept any dynasty they propose _ : but it be not-listened to then come the horror of arad -lrb- \* -rrb- and destroy all we faith in monarchy so the last of the three book be burn -lrb- footnote \* : in arad the hungarian general who surrender by görgy 's persuasion be hang or shoot and simultaneously bathyanyus who have be arrest when he come as a ambassador of peace be judge anew and murder by a second court-martial -rrb- and so wherever man 's reasonable expectation be not fulfil it can not be know where they fluctuation will end every man who be anxious for the preservation of person and property should help the world in obtain rational freedom : if it be not obtain mankind will search after other form of action totally subversive of all exist social order and where the excitement will subside i do not know man like I who merely wish to establish political freedom will in such circumstance lose all they influence and other will get influence who may become dangerous to all establish interest whatsoever \* \* \* \* \* iv -- legitimacy of hungarian independence -lrb- when kossuth have land at staten island thus for the first time set he foot on american soil he be meet by a deputation which make a address to he he reply as follow -lrb- dec 5th 1851 -rrb- -rrb- : -- lady and gentleman : the twelve hour that i have have the happiness to stand on you shore give I augury that during my stay in the united state i shall have a pleasant duty to perform in answer the generous spirit of you people i hope however that you will consider that i be in the first moment of a hard task -- to address you intelligent people in a tongue foreign to I you will not expect from I a elaborate speech but will be contented with a few warmly-felt word citizen accept my fervent thanks for you generous welcome and my blessing upon you sanction of my hope you have most truly state what they be when you announce the destiny of you glorious country and tell I that from it the spirit of liberty will go forth and achieve the freedom of the world yes citizen these be the hope which have induce I in a most eventful period to cross the atlantic i confidently hope that as you have anticipate my wish by the expression of you generous sentiment so you will agree with I that the spirit of liberty have to go forth not only spiritually but materially from you glorious country that spirit be a power for deed but be yet no _ deed _ in itself despotism and oppression never yet be beat except by heroic resistance that be a sad necessity -- but it be a necessity nevertheless i have so learn it out of the great book of history i hope the people of the united state will remember that in the hour of _ they _ nation 's struggle it receive from europe _ more _ than kind wish it receive material aid from other in time past and it will doubtless now impart its mighty agency to achieve the liberty of other land citizen i thank you for have address I not in the language of party but in the language of liberty which be that of the united state i come hither in the name of hungary to entreat not from any _ party _ among you but from you _ whole nation _ a generous protection for my country and for that very reason neither will i intermeddle with any of you party question in england i often avowed this principle inasmuch as the very mission on which i come be to ask that the right of every nation to arrange its domestic concern may be respect notwithstanding this i be sorry to see that before my arrival i have be charge with intermeddle with you presidential election because in one of my address in england i mention the name of you fellow-citizen mr walker as one of the candidate for the presidency i confess with warm gratitude that mr walker utter such sentiment in england as if happily they be also those of the united state will enable I to declare that hungary and europe be free therefore i feel deeply indebted to he but in no respect do i mix myself up with you election i consider no man honest who do not observe towards other nation the principle which he desire to be observe towards he own : and therefore i will not interfere in you domestic question allow I citizen to advert to one expression of you kind address personal to myself you name I kossuth governor of hungary my nomination to be governor be not to gratify ambition never perhaps do i feel sadder than at the moment when that title be confer upon I for i compare my feeble faculty and its high responsibility it be therefore not from ambition that i thank you for the title but because the title rest upon we declaration of independence and by acknowledge it as mine you recognize the rightfulness and validity of that declaration and gentleman i frankly declare that you whole people be bind in honor and duty to recognize it at this moment there be no other legitimate exist law in hungary it be not the proclamation of a man or of a party it be the solemn declaration of the whole nation in _ congress _ assemble it be sanction by _ every village _ and by _ every municipality _ no counter-proclamation have go forth from hungary it have be overturn solely by the invasion of a ambitious _ foreign _ power the czar of russium who can no more legitimately make or unmake a governor of hungary than general santa anna if in you late war he have force he way to washington could have unmade president taylor none of you will admit that violence can destroy righteousness : it can but establish unlawful unrightful _ fact _ if so -- if you own people and not foreign invader be the source of rightful law to _ you _ -- you must in consistency recognize _ we _ independence as legitimate and its declaration as we still rightful law as to the praise which you be so kind as to bestow upon I it be no affectation in I when i declare that i be not conscious of have any other merit than that of be a plain straightforward man a faithful friend of freedom a good patriot and these quality gentleman be so natural to _ every _ honest man that it be scarcely worth while to speak of they for i can not conceive how a man with understanding and with a sound heart can be anything else than a good patriot and a lover of freedom yet my humble capacity have not preserve I from calumny scarcely have i arrive here when i learn that i have be charge in the united state with be a _ irreligious man _ so long as despot exist and have the means to pay they will find man to calumniate those who be oppose to tyranny but suppose i be the most dishonest creature in the world in the name of all that be sacred _ what would that matter in respect to the cause of hungary _ would that cause become less just less righteous less worthy of you sympathy because i for instance be a bad man no i believe you it be not a question in regard to any individual here it be a question with regard to a just cause the cause of a country worthy to take its place in the great family of the free nation of the world until i learn that you refuse to recognize nation whenever they governor fall short of religious perfection i need not care much about attack on my mere personality but one thing i can scarcely comprehend -- that the press -- that mighty vehicle of justice and champion of human rights -- could have find a organ and that in the united state which -lrb- to say nothing of personal calumny -rrb- should degrade itself to assert that it be not the people of hungary it be not myself and my coadjutor that contend for liberty but it be the emperor of austrium who be the champion of liberty do not give it groan gentleman but rather thank it for there can be no better service to any cause than for its opponent to manifest that they have nothing to say but what be ridiculous that _ must _ have be a sacred and just cause whose detractor need to assert that the emperor of austrium be the champion of freedom throughout he own dominion and throughout the european continent i thank you that you have give I full proof that all these calumny have affect neither you judgment nor you heart as this will be the place whence i shall start back for europe i shall once more have the happiness of address you publicly and bidding you a affectionate adieu : -- hope then to be able to thank you for _ act _ as i now thank you for _ sentiment _ \* \* \* \* \* declaration of independence by the hungarian nation -lrb- the reader may be glad to possess the most important portion of this celebrated document the opponent of kossuth have of late pretend that the deposition of the hapsburg _ cause _ the overthrow of hungary but the deposition be not carry until austrium be thoroughly beat and russium _ have engage _ to give she utmost aid this finally unite all hungary at no earlier period would hungary have act with full unanimity in so decisive a step to have delay it longer would not have avert russian invasion and would have cause deep discontent in hungary nothing but the wilful disobedience of görgey who waste a month at buda at this very crisis save the hapsburg from be conquer in vienna before the russian army could possibly come up -rrb- we the legally-constituted representative of the hungarian nation assemble in diet do by these present solemnly proclaim in maintenance of the inalienable natural rights of hungary with all its appurtenance and dependency to occupy the position of a independent european state that the house of lorraine-hapsburg as perjure in the sight of god and man have forfeit its right to the hungarian throne at the same time we feel ourselves bind in duty to make know the motive and reason which have impel we to this decision that the civilized world may learn we have not take this step out of overweening confidence in we own wisdom or out of revolutionary excitement but that it be a act of the last necessity adopt to preserve from utter destruction a nation persecute to the limit of the most enduring patience three hundred year have pass since the hungarian nation by free election place the house of austrium upon its throne in accordance with stipulation make on both side and ratify by treaty these three hundred year have be for the country a period of uninterrupted suffer the creator have bless this country with all the element of wealth and happiness its area of one hundred and ten thousand square mile present in varied profusion innumerable source of prosperity its population numbering nearly fifteen million feel the glow of youthful strength within its vein and have show temper and docility which warrant its proving at once the main organ of civilization in eastern europe and the guardian of that civilization when attack never be a more grateful task appoint to a reign dynasty by the dispensation of providence than that which devolve upon the house of lorraine-hapsburg it would have suffice to do nothing to impede the development of the country have this be the rule observe hungary would now rank among the most prosperous nation it be only necessary that it should not envy the hungarian the moderate share of constitutional liberty which they timidly maintain during the difficulty of a thousand year with rare fidelity to they sovereign and the house of hapsburg might long have count this nation among the most faithful adherent of the throne this dynasty however which can at no epoch point to a ruler who base he power on the freedom of the people adopt a course towards this nation from father to son which deserve the appellation of perjury the house of austrium unite all in a common sink of slavery foiled in this effort by the untiring vigilance of the nation it direct its endeavor to lame the power to check the progress of hungary cause it to minister to the gain of the province of austrium but only to the extent which enable those province to bear the load of taxation with which the prodigality of the imperial house weigh they down have first deprive those province of all constitutional means of remonstrate against a policy which be not base upon the welfare of the subject but solely tend to maintain despotism and crush liberty in every country of europe it have frequently happen that the hungarian nation in despite of this systematize tyranny have be oblige to take up arm in self-defence although constantly victorious in these constitutional struggle yet so moderate have the nation ever be in its use of the victory so strongly have it confide in the king 's plighted word that it have ever lay down arm as soon as the king by new compact and fresh oath have guarantee the duration of its rights and liberty but every new compact be as futile as those which precede it each oath which fall from the royal lip be but a renewal of previous perjury the policy of the house of austrium which aim at destroy the independence of hungary as a state have be pursue unaltered for three hundred year it be in vain that the hungarian nation shed its government of that dynasty in hungary present but a unbroken series of perjured deed from generation to generation in spite of such treatment the hungarian nation have all along respect the tie by which it be unite to this dynasty and in now decree its expulsion from the throne it act under the natural law of self-preservation be drive to pronounce this sentence by the full conviction that the house of lorraine-hapsburg be compass the destruction of hungary as a independent state : so that this dynasty have be the first to tear the band by which it be unite to the hungarian nation and to confess that it have tear they in the face of europe for many cause a nation be justified before god and man in expel a reign dynasty among such be the following : 1 when the dynasty form alliance with the enemy of the country with robber or partizan chieftain to oppress the nation : 2 when it attempt to annihilate the independence of the country and its constitution support on oath by attack with a armed force the people who have commit no act of revolt : 3 when the integrity of a country which the sovereign have swear to maintain be violate and its resource cut away : 4 when foreign army be employ to murder the people and to oppress they liberty each of the grounds here enumerate would justify the exclusion of a dynasty from the throne but the house of lorraine-hapsburg be unexampled in the compass of its perjury and have commit every one of these crime against the nation \*\*\* in former time a govern council under the name of the royal hungarian stadtholdership the president of hungary have ostensibly a independent government the despotic vienna cabinet dispose at will of the money and blood of the people for foreign purpose postpone we commercial interest to the success of courtly cabal injurious to the welfare of the people so that we be exclude from all connection with the other country of the world and be degrade to the position of a colony the mode of govern by a to rise in rebellion against the law of the country and nominate he ban of croatium a kingdom belong to the kingdom of hungary \*\*\* the ban revolt therefore in the name of the emperor and rebel legal power _ debreczin April _ 14 1849 \* \* \* \* \* v -- statement of principle and aim -lrb- _ castle garden new york dec 6th _ -rrb- after apology for he weakness through the effect of the sea kossuth continue : -- citizen much as i want some hour of rest much as i need to become acquaint with my ground before i enter publicly on matter of business i yet take it for a duty of honor to respond at once to you generous welcome i have to thank the people the congress and the government of the united state for my liberation i must not try to express what i feel when i -- a wanderer -- but not the less the legitimate official chief of hungary -- first see the glorious flag of the stripe and star flutter over my head -- when i see around I the gallant officer and the crew of the _ mississippus _ frigate -- most of they worthy representative of true american principle american greatness american generosity it be not a mere chance which cast the star-spangled banner around I it be you protect will the united state of america conscious of they glorious call as well as of they power declare by this unparalleled act they resolve to become the protector of human rights to see a powerful vessel of america come to far asia in order to break the chain by which the mightiest despot of europe fetter the activity of a exile magyar whose name disturb they sleep -- to be restore by such a protection to freedom and activity -- you may well conceive be intensely feel by I as indeed i still feel it other _ speak _ -- you _ act _ and i be free you act and at this act of yours tyrant tremble humanity shout out with joy the magyar nation crushed but not broken raise its head with resolution and with hope and the brilliancy of you star be greet by europe 's oppressed million as the morning star of liberty now gentleman you must be aware how great my gratitude must be you have restore I to life -- in restore I to activity and should my life by the blessing of the almighty still prove useful to my fatherland and to humanity it will be you merit -- it will be you work may you and you country be bless for it you generous part in my liberation be take by the world for the revelation of the fact that the united state be resolve not to allow the despot of the world to trample on oppressed humanity that be why my liberation be cheer from sweden to portugal as a ray of hope even those nation which most desire my presence in europe now have say to I hasten on hasten on to the great free rich and powerful people of the united state and bring over its brotherly aid to the cause of you country so intimately connect with european liberty and here i stand to plead the cause of common human rights before you great republic humble as i be god the almighty have select I to represent the cause of humanity before you my warrant hereto be write in the sympathy and confidence of all who be oppressed and of all who as you elder sister the british nation sympathize with the oppressed it be write in the hope and expectation you have entitle the world to entertain by liberating I out of my prison but it have please the almighty to make out of my humble self yet another opportunity for a thing which may prove a happy turning-point in the destiny of the world i bring you a brotherly greet from the people of great britain i speak not in a official character impart by diplomacy whose secrecy be the curse of the world but i be the harbinger of the public spirit of the people which i witness pronounce itself in the most decide manner openly -- that the people of england unite to you with enlighten brotherly love as it be unite in blood -- conscious of you strength as it be conscious of its own have for ever abandon every sentiment of irritation and rivalry and desire the brotherly alliance of the united state to secure to every nation the sovereign right to dispose of itself and to protect that right against encroach arrogance it desire to league with you against the league of despot and with you to stand sponsor at the approach baptism of european liberty now gentleman i have state my position i be a straightforward man i be a republican i have avow it openly in monarchical but free england and be happy to state that i have lose nothing by this avowal there i hope i shall not lose here in republican america by that frankness which must be one of the chief quality of every republican so i beg leave openly to state the follow point : first that i take it to be duty of honor and principle not to meddle with any party-question of you own domestic affair secondly i profess my admiration for the glorious principle of union on which stand the mighty pyramid of you greatness take my ground on this constitutional fact it be not to a party but to you united people that i will confidently address my humble request within the limit of you law i will use every honest exertion to gain you effectual sympathy and you financial material and political aid for my country 's freedom and independence and entreat the realization of the hope which you generosity have raise and therefore thirdly i frankly state that my aim be to restore my fatherland to the full enjoyment of she own independence which have be legitimately declare and can not have lose its rightfulness by the violent invasion of foreign russian arm what can be oppose to it the frown of mr hulsemann -- the anger of that satellite of the czar call francis-joseph of austrium and the immense danger -lrb- with which some european and american papers threaten you -rrb- lest you minister at vienna receive he passport and mr hulsemann leave washington should i be receive in my official capacity now as to you minister at vienna how you can reconcile the let he stay there with you opinion of the cause of hungary i do not know for the present absolutist atmosphere of europe be not very propitious to american principle but as to mr hulsemann do not believe that he would be so ready to leave washington he have extremely well digest the caustic word which mr webster have administer to he so gloriously i know that you public spirit would never allow any responsible depository of the executive power to be regulate in its policy by all the hulsemann or all the francis-joseph in the world but it be also my agreeable conviction that the highminded government of the united state share warmly the sentiment of the people it have prove it by execute in a ready and dignified manner the resolution of congress on behalf of my liberation it have prove it by call on the congress to consider how i shall be receive and even this morning i be honor by the express order of the government with a official salute from the battery of the united state in a manner in which accord to the military rule only a high official personage can be greet i come not to you glorious shore to enjoy a happy rest -- i come not to gather triumph of personal distinction but as a humble petitioner in my country 's name as its freely choose constitutional leader to entreat you generous aid i have no other claim than those which the oppressed principle of freedom have to the aid of victorious liberty if you consider these claim not sufficient for you active and effectual sympathy then let I know at once that the hope have fail with which europe have look to you great mighty and glorious republic -- let I know it at once that i may hasten back and say to the oppressed nation let we fight forsake and single-handed the battle of leonida let we trust to god to we right and to we good sword for we have no other help on earth but if you generous republican heart be animated by the high principle of freedom and of the community in human destiny -- if you have the will as undoubtedly you have the power to support the cause of freedom against the sacrilegious league of despotism then give I some day of calm reflection to become acquaint with the ground upon which i stand -- let I take kind advice as to my course -- let I learn whether any step have be already take in favor of that cause which i have the honor to represent and then let I have a new opportunity to expound before you my humble request in a practical way i confidently hope mr mayor the corporation and citizen of the empire city will grant I a second opportunity if this be you generous will then let I take this for a boon of happier day and let I add with a sigh of thanksgive to the almighty god that providence have select you glorious country to be the pillar of freedom as it be already the asylum to oppressed humanity i be tell that i shall have the high honor to review you patriotic militia my heart throb at the idea of see this gallant army enlist on the side of freedom against despotism the world would then soon be free and you the savior of humanity citizen of new york it be under you protection that i place the sacred cause of freedom and the independence of hungary \* \* \* \* \* vi -- reply to the baltimore address -lrb- _ dec 10th _ 1851 -rrb- mr henry p brook chairman of the committee of the baltimore city council come forward and after congratulating kossuth upon he release from peril and arrival in america he present the follow resolution of the council write on parchment : -- in city council whereas it be understand that loui kossuth the illustrious hungarian patriot and exile be about seek a asylum upon we shore and whereas it be believe that the city of baltimore in common with the whole people of the united state feel a deep and abiding interest in the cause of freedom wherever it be assail and entertain the most sincere regret for the unfortunate condition of hungary and whereas in the reception of kossuth a opportunity be offer of express we sympathy for the cause of hungarian independence -- of record we detestation of the unholy coalition by which that gallant people have be crushed and of evince we admiration of the noble conduct of the turkish sultan in refuse to deliver to the despot of europe that illustrious exile and patriot whom it be about to be we privilege and pride to receive as it befit the choose people of liberty to receive one who have so nobly battle and suffer in that sacred cause therefore -- _ resolve _ by the mayor and city council of baltimore that we look to the arrival of kossuth upon we shore with mingled feeling of satisfaction and regret -- satisfaction that we be enable to afford a safe asylum to a illustrious patriot -- regret that the cause of liberty should give birth to such necessity _ resolve _ that we sympathize fully with the hungarian in they important struggle for independence but mindful of that providence which crown we own effort for liberty with success trust yet to behold that glorious future which they noble leader so eloquently predict for he beloved country _ resolve _ that we regard the alliance with russium and austrium for the purpose of crush the spirit of liberty in hungary as a fit accompaniment in the annals of time for the infamous partition of unfortunate poland by the same tyrannical power each alike worthy of the execration of the civilized world _ resolve _ that we cordially welcome kossuth and he exile companion to the full enjoyment of american liberty and a asylum beyond the reach of european despotism _ resolve _ further that a joint committee of five from each branch of the city council be appoint whose duty it shall be in conjunction with the mayor in the event of they arrival in we city to tender to they appropriate public token of we esteem and admiration for they gallant conduct as well as of we sympathy for they suffering and they cause committee under the last resolution -- first branch : henry p brooke john dukehart j hanson thoma david blanford john thomas morri second branch : jacob j cohen w b morri hugh a cooper jame c ninde geo a lover john h j jerome mayor john s brown president of first branch hugh bolton president of second branch city of baltimore state of maryland unite state of america oct 28 ad 1851 -lrb- after hear several other -- complimentary address kossuth in a few minute reply he begin with apology and then proceed -rrb- : -- permit I to say that in my opinion the word glory should be blot out from the dictionary in respect to individual and only leave for use in respect to nation whatever a man can do for he country even though he should live a long life and have the strongest faculty would not be too much : for he ought to use he utmost exertion and he utmost power in return for the gift he receive whatever a man can do on behalf of he country and of humanity would never be so much as he duty call upon he to do still less so much as to merit the use of the word glory in regard to himself once more i say that duty belong to the man and glory to the nation when a honest man do he duty to he own country and become a patriot he act for all humanity and do he duty to mankind you have bestow great attention upon the cause of hungary and the subject be here well understand generally which be a benefit to I i declare to you all that i find more exact knowledge of the hungarian cause here than in any other place i have be yet i be astonish to see in a report of the proceedings of the united state senate that a member rise and say that we be not struggle for the principle of freedom and of liberty but rather for the support of we ancient charter this gentleman be a misrepresentation of we cause there be a truth in the assertion that we be struggle for we _ ancient rights _ for the right of self-government be a ancient right the right of self-government be ours a thousand year ago and have be guarantee to we by the coronation the immense majority of you conscious of you noble vocation and instinct with the generosity of freedom protect we sacred rights against the dark plot of tyranny you independent press have likewise prove that its freedom be the most efficient protection even against calumny a far better one than restrictive prevention which condemn the human intellect to eternal minority i address you gentleman with the greater joy because through you i have the invaluable benefit of reach the whole of you great glorious and free people eighty year ago the immortal franklin 's own press be almost the only one in the colony : now you have above three thousand newspaper with a circulation of five million of copy i be tell that the journal of new york state alone exceed in number those of all the rest of except in the united state there be scarcely anywhere a practical freedom of the press indeed concern norway i be not quite aware but throughout the european continent you know how the press be fetter in france under nominally republican government all the fruit of victorious revolution be nipt by the blast grip of _ centralize _ power -- legislative and administrative omnipotence the independence state that queen victorium be no lawful queen and all those who rule ought to be hang but man only laugh at the foolish extravagance nevertheless i hope the generous people of great britain will not be offend when i say that they press be not practically free its freedom be not real for it be not a _ common benefit _ to all : it be but a particular benefit that be a _ privilege _ taxation there forbid the use of newspaper to the poor absence of taxation enable you journal to be publish at one tenth or even one twentieth of the english price : hence several of you daily papers reach from thirty to sixty thousand reader while in england one paper alone be on this scale -- the london ` time ' which circulate thirty thousand perhaps such be the condition of you press in address you i address a whole people nor only so but a whole intelligent people the wide diffusion of intelligence among you be in fact prove by the immense circulation of you journal it be not solely the cheap price which render you press a common benefit and not a mere privilege to the richer but it be the universality of public instruction it be glorious to know that in this flourish young city alone nearly a hundred thousand child receive public education annually do you know gentleman what i consider to be you most glorious monument if it be as i have read that when you engineer draw geometrical speak on the question of nationality a false theory of which play so mischievous a part in the destiny of europe no word have be more misrepresent than the word nationality which be become in the hand of absolutism a dangerous instrument against liberty let I ask you gentleman : be you the people of the united state a _ nation _ or not have you a _ national _ government or not you answer yes : and yet you be not all of one blood nor of one language million of you speak english other french german italian spanish danish and even several indian dialect : yet you be a nation neither you central government nor those of separate state nor you municipality legislate or administer in every language speak among you yet you have a national government now suppose many of you be strike with the curse of babel and exclaim this union be a oppression we law we institution we state and city government be a oppression what be union to we what be rights what avail law what be freedom what be geography what be community of interest to we they be all nothing language be everything let we divide the union divide the state divide the very city divide the whole territory accord to language let the people of every language become a separate state : for every nation have a right to national life and to we the language and nothing else be the nationality unless the state be found upon language its organization be tyranny what then would become of you great union what of you constitution the glorious legacy of you greatest man what of those immortal star on mankind 's moral sky what would become of you country itself whence the spirit of freedom soar into light and rise hope irradiate the future of humanity what would become of this grand mighty complex of you republic should she integrity ever be rent by the fanatic of language where now she walk among the rise temple of liberty and happiness she soon would tread upon ruin and mourn over human hope but happy art then free nation of america found on the only solid basis -- liberty a principle steady as the world eternal as the truth universal for every climate for every time like providence tyrant be not in the midst of you to throw the apple of discord and raise hatred in this national family hatred of _ race _ that curse of humanity that venomous ally of despotism glorious it be to see the oppress of diverse country -- diverse in language history habit -- wander to these shore and become member of this great nation regenerate by the principle of common liberty if language alone make a nation then there be no great nation on earth : for there be no country whose population be count by million but speak more than one language no it be not language only community of interest of rights of duty of history but chiefly community of institution by which a population vary perhaps in tongue and race be bind together through daily intercourse in the town which be the centre and home of commerce and industry : -- besides these the very mountain-ranges the system of river and stream -- the soil the dust of which be mingle with the mortal remains of those ancestor who bleed on the same field for the same interest the common inheritance of glory and of woe the community of law and institution common freedom or common oppression : -- all this enter into the complex idea of nationality that this be instinctively feel by the common sense of the people nowhere be more manifestly show than at this very moment in my native land hungary be declare by franci joseph of austrium _ no more to exist _ as a nation no more as a state it be and be put under martial law stranger alien to we law and history as well as to we tongue rule now where we father live and we brother bleed to be a hungarian be become almost a crime in we own native land well : to justify before the world the extinction of hungary the partition of its territory and the reincorporating of the dissect limb into the common body of servitude the treacherous dynasty be anxious to show that the hungarian be in a minority in they own land they hope that intimidation and terrorism would induce even the very magyar to disavow they language and birth they order a census of race to be make they perform it with the iron rule of martial law and deal so arbitrarily that thousand of woman and man who profess to be magyar who profess not to know any other language than the magyar be notwithstanding all they protestation put down as sclave serb german or wallachian because they name have not quite a hungarian sound and still what be the issue of this malignant plot that of the twelve million of inhabitant of hungary proper the magyar turn out to be more than eight million some two million more than we know the case really be the people instinctively feel that the tyrant have the design through the pretext of language to destroy the existence of the complex nation and it meet the tyrannic plot as if it answer we be and must be a nation and if the tyrant take language only for the mark of nationality then we be all magyar and mark well gentleman this happen not under my governorship but under the rule of austrian martial law the cabinet of vienna become furious it think of a new census but prudent man tell they that a new census would give the whole twelve million as magyar thus no new census be take but on the european continent there unhappily have grow up a school which bind the idea of nationality to the idea of language only and join political pretension to it there be some who advocate the theory that exist state must cease and the territory of the world be divide anew by language and nation separate by tongue you be aware that this idea if it be not impracticable would be a curse to humanity -- a deathblow to civilization and progress and throw back mankind by century it would be a eternal source of strife and war : for there be a holy almost religious tie by which man 's heart be bind to he home and no man would ever consent to abandon he native land only because he neighbor speak another language than himself he heart claim that sacred spot where the ash of he father lie -- where he to respect to love and to venerate the body of man now present to you about five thousand in number represent the first division of new york state militia the division enrol about fifty thousand man in this city and upon staten island and the law of we state only impose upon the general body the duty of appear armed and equipped once in each year at a annual parade appoint for that purpose but out of this large number the law provide for the organization of those who be willing and desirous to acquire that degree of military science to fit they upon any sudden emergency of domestic insurrection or of foreign aggression to sustain the law and support the institution of we country they uniform and equip themselves at they own expense and they serve without pay satisfy with the consciousness that they be discharge a duty to they country and qualify themselves to sustain the honor of we flag and the freedom win by we father they represent fairly all class of we citizen we international law which you have recently so eloquently and ably expound -- that one nation should not interfere with the domestic concern of another establish this great and just principle and hungary would again assume she station among the nation of the earth -- free and independent establish this great principle and germany and italy would also soon be free sir we believe in this great principle we believe it to be a principle of justice and humanity we believe it to be the inalienable right of every people to establish such form of government as be best adapt to they condition and as they may deem best calculate to ensure they own rights liberty and pursuit of happiness and we believe that this great principle of international law should be the basis of the intercourse of nation and that we have no more right to make free with the form of government of other nation than with they form of religion but this principle be concede and establish how be it to be enforce how be the despotic dynasty of europe to be prevent from lend they combine energy to crush every germ of freedom amongst those who if leave to themselves would like hungary be free and independent solely by the method which you have so ably develop solely by induce those nation which be strong enough to maintain the principle of international law -- to unite in they support and by such union effectually to guarantee the peace of the world to effect this most desirable object you have adopt the true method you would operate upon the public opinion and public opinion operating upon free government create and establish public and international law but when we see this great principle of non-intervention violate -- when we see a free and united people crushed and trample upon by glorious principle can only be triumphant when the nation of the earth shall become free from oppression because it be only under the protection of free institution -- a free press free controversy freedom of speech and free popular education -- where it be you privilege to preach and that of the neighbor to hear -- that the political independence of a people can be preserve oppression be everywhere accompany by the demoralization of the mass and they adoption of infidelity or fanaticism while under the teaching of freedom religion become a growth of the soul he would urge they to go liberty to all mankind thus we may see that the triumph of genuine liberty can best be secure by recognize religion as the true basis of the law of nation he who shall be instrumental in incorporate this grand doctrine among those law will be equal or perhaps superior to a luther or a melancthon a calvin or a huss a cranmer or any other of the world 's greatest reformer the people of this republic have all this within they grasp and he hope the almighty would hasten the day when it shall be do he have often hear that the people of this country love to be call a great people and he have many time hear they call a great people to _ be _ a great people however the people of this country must really _ act _ as a great people he urge upon the minister of the gospel that they should warn they flock against the horrid doctrine of _ materialism _ nothing be more hostile to national greatness than when the poor see the rich govern only by pecuniary consideration -- leave nothing for the march -lrb- _ farewell speech at st loui march 15th _ -rrb- lady and gentleman : to-day be the fourth anniversary of the revolution in hungary anniversary of revolution be almost always connect with the recollection of some patriot death-fallen on that day like the spartan at thermopylae martyr of devotion to they fatherland almost in every country there be some proud cemetery or some modest tomb-stone adorn on such a day by a garland of evergreen the pious offering of patriotic tenderness i past the last night in a sleepless dream and my soul wander on the magnetic wing of the past home to my beloved bleeding land and i saw in the dead of the night dark veil shape with the paleness of eternal grief upon they brow but terrible in the tearless silence of that grief glide over the churchyard of hungary and kneel down to the head of the grave and deposit the pious tribute of green and cypress upon they and after a short prayer rise with clenched fist and gnash tooth and then show a pious remembrance to the beloved to-day a smile on the lip of a magyar be take for a crime of defiance to tyranny and a tear in he eye be equivalent to a revolt and yet i have see with the eye down such be the dream of my wake soul and i prayed and such be my prayer : father if thou deemest I worthy take the cup from my people and give it in they stead to I and there be a whisper around I the 15th of march the anniversary of we revolution have not the stain of a single drop of blood we the elect of the nation sit on that morning busily but quietly in the legislative hall of old presburg and without any flood of eloquence pass we law in short word that the people shall be free the burden of feudality cease the peasant become free proprietor that equality of duty equality of rights shall be the fundamental law and civil political social and religious liberty the common property of all the people whatever tongue it may speak or in whatever church pray and that a national ministry shall execute these law and guard with its responsibility the chartered ancient independence of we fatherland two day before austrium 's brave people in vienna have break its yoke and sum up a national guard the window be illuminate and bonfire burnt and when these tiding return back to presburg blended with the cheer from vienna they warm the chill of we house of lord who readily agree to the law we propose and there be rejoice throughout the land for the first time for century the farmer awake with the pleasant feeling that he time be now he own -- for the first time go out to till he field with the console thought that the ninth part of he harvest will not be take by the landlord and the tenth by the bishop both have fully resign they feudal portion and the air be brighten by fight like demi-god seven great victory we have gain in that month of march on this very day the remains of the first 10000 russian flee over the frontier of transylvanium to tell at home how heavily the blow fall from free hungarian arm it be in that very month that one evening i lay down in the bed whence in the morning windischgrätz have rise : and from the battle-field -lrb- isaszeg -rrb- i hasten to the congress at debreczin to tell the representative of the nation : it be time to declare we national independence because it be really achieve the hapsburg have not the power to contradict honorable secretary of state express that i consider the struggle for we national independence not yet finish and that i would devote my regain liberty to the cause of my fatherland _ nearly three \* xlii -- panegyric of massachusett -lrb- _ speech at faneuil hall _ -rrb- kossuth enter boston on the 27th April escort by twenty-nine company of infantry and four of artillery in the midst of flag governor then conduct kossuth to the senate where he be warmly welcome by the president general wilson and thence again to the house of representative where the speaker mr bank address he in word of high honor in the name of the representative to each of these address kossuth reply but the substance of he speech have scarcely sufficient novelty to present here on the evening of the 29th of April word on the ancient institution of hungary i have often hear it say that the people of europe be incapable of self-government let I speak of the people of hungary to show whether they be capable of self-government or not in thirty-six year with god 's help and through you generous aid the free people of hungary will celebrate the 1000th anniversary of the establishment of they home -- the millennium of hungary in europe yes gentleman may i hope that celebration will take place under the blessing of liberty in the year 1889 it be a long period -- one thousand year -- and oh how it have teem with adversity to my countryman and yet through this long time amid all adversity there be no period when the people of hungary do not resist despotism we boast be that through the vicissitude of a thousand year there be not a moment when the popular will and the legal authority have sanction the rule of absolutism and gentleman what other people for 1000 year have not consent to be rule by despotism even in the nineteenth century i be glad to look back to the wisdom of we father through a thousand year -- who lay down for hungarian institution a basis which for all eternity must remain true this basis be upon that latin proverb _ nil de nobis sine nobis _ -- nothing about we without we that be to claim that every man should have a full share in the sovereignty of the people and a full share in the rights belong to he nation in other time a theory be get up to convince the people that they might have a share in _ legislation _ just so far as to control that legislation but deny the right of the people to control the _ executive _ power the hungarian people never adopt that theory they ever claim a full share in the _ executive _ as well as in the legislative and judicial power out of this idea of government rise the municipal system of hungary in respect to hungarian aristocracy you must not consider it in the same light as the aristocracy of england the word _ nobleman _ in hungary originally be equivalent to _ soldier _ every man who defend he country be a nobleman and every man who have a vote be call to defend he country i believe the duty of defend a man 's country and also political right should be common after we people have conquer a home the leader take the lion 's share of course but it should be consider that those who have the largest share of the property be compel to furnish soldier accord to the extent of they possession therefore such man give a part of they land to people to cultivate and desire aid of they whenever the necessity for war come so all who defend they country be consider nobleman hungary be divide into fifty-two county but not county like yours -- some of they be so populous as to be comparable to you state contain perhaps half a million or more of people and those who become the aristocracy in some of these county amount to 35000 in every county be a fortress and whenever defense become necessary the rich man go into these fortress under they own banner and the other go under the king 's color and be command by the sheriff of the county who might be here governor -- at least who be the chief of the executive certain of the city be raise to constitutional rights a smaller city if surround by fortification or if a important post be represent in the diet whilst larger place if not post of importance for national defense be represent only by the county delegate every place that have the element of defense have political rights so it come to pass that the aristocracy be not a few man but half a million i have contend to beat down this barrier of aristocracy before the revolution in municipal government only the nobility have a share -- they only be the man who could vote : but the change be easy the frame of self-government be ready we have only to say _ the people _ instead of _ the nobility _ have the right to vote and so in one day we bury aristocracy never to rise again each county elect its representative to the diet and have the right of intercourse with other county by means of letter on all matter of importance to these county and therefore we fifty-two primary council be normal school of public spirit we elect we judicatory and executive and the government have not a right to send instruction or order to we executive and if a order come which we consider to be inconsistent with we constitutional rights it be not send to the executive but to the council and therefore the arbitrary order of the government could not be execute because they come not into the hand of the executive thus be we council barrier against oppression when the french take saragossa it be not enough to take the city -- they have to take every house so also _ we _ go on and though some county might accept the arbitrary order of the government some resist and by discuss in they letter to the other county the point of right enlighten they and it be see that when the last house in saragossa have be beat down the first stand erect again in consequence of the democratic nature of we institution we council be we grand jury but after have elect we judge we choose several man in rain a everflowing influence and secondly in contradiction to this universally adopt creed i have meet in many quarter a propensity to believe that it be conservative wisdom not to take any active part in the regulation of the outward world these two thing do not agree if that be the destiny of america which you all believe to be then that destiny can never be fulfil by act the part of passive spectator and by this very passivity grant a charter to ambitious czar to dispose of the condition of the world i have meet distinguished man trust so much to the operative power of you institution and of you _ example _ that they really believe they will make they way throughout the world merely by they _ moral influence _ but there be one thing those gentleman have disregard in they philanthropic reliance and that be that the ray of the sun never yet make its way by itself through well-closed shutter and door -- they must be draw open that the bless ray of the sun may get in i have never yet hear of a despot who yield to the moral influence of liberty the ground of concord itself be a evidence of it the door and shutter of oppression must be open by bayonet that the bless ray of you institution may penetrate into the dark dwelling-house of oppressed humanity there be man who believe the position of a power on earth will come to you by itself but oh do not trust to this fallacy a position never come by itself it must be take and take it never will be by passivity the martyr who have hallowed by they blood the ground of concord trust themselves and occupy the place
